<p><i><b>Alice in Wonderland</b></i> is a 2010 American <a href="/wiki/Fantasy_film" title="Fantasy film">fantasy film</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> directed by <a href="/wiki/Tim_Burton" title="Tim Burton">Tim Burton</a> and written by <a href="/wiki/Linda_Woolverton" title="Linda Woolverton">Linda Woolverton</a>. Released by <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Pictures" title="Walt Disney Pictures">Walt Disney Pictures</a>, the film stars <a href="/wiki/Mia_Wasikowska" title="Mia Wasikowska">Mia Wasikowska</a> as <a href="/wiki/Alice_(Alice%27s_Adventures_in_Wonderland)#Tim_Burton_film" title="Alice (Alice's Adventures in Wonderland)">Alice Kingsleigh</a> with <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Depp" title="Johnny Depp">Johnny Depp</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anne_Hathaway" title="Anne Hathaway">Anne Hathaway</a> and <a href="/wiki/Helena_Bonham_Carter" title="Helena Bonham Carter">Helena Bonham Carter</a>. The film was shot in the United Kingdom and the United States.</p>
<p>The story is inspired by the English author <a href="/wiki/Lewis_Carroll" title="Lewis Carroll">Lewis Carroll</a>'s 1865 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fantasy_novel" title="Fantasy novel">fantasy novel</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Alice%27s_Adventures_in_Wonderland" title="Alice's Adventures in Wonderland">Alice's Adventures in Wonderland</a></i> and its 1871 sequel <i><a href="/wiki/Through_the_Looking-Glass" title="Through the Looking-Glass">Through the Looking-Glass</a></i>. Wasikowska plays a nineteen-year-old <a href="/wiki/Alice_(Alice%27s_Adventures_in_Wonderland)" title="Alice (Alice's Adventures in Wonderland)">Alice</a>. She is told that she can restore the <a href="/wiki/White_Queen_(Through_the_Looking-Glass)" title="White Queen (Through the Looking-Glass)">White Queen</a> to her throne because she is the only one who can slay the <a href="/wiki/Jabberwocky" title="Jabberwocky">Jabberwock</a>, a dragon-like creature that is controlled by the <a href="/wiki/Red_Queen_(Through_the_Looking-Glass)" title="Red Queen (Through the Looking-Glass)">Red Queen</a> and terrorizes Underland's inhabitants.</p>
<p>The film premiered in London at the <a href="/wiki/Odeon_Leicester_Square" title="Odeon Leicester Square">Odeon Leicester Square</a> on February 25, 2010, and was released in Australia on March 4, 2010 and the following day in the United Kingdom and the United States through <a href="/wiki/IMAX" title="IMAX">IMAX 3D</a> and <a href="/wiki/Disney_Digital_3-D" title="Disney Digital 3-D">Disney Digital 3D</a> as well as in traditional theaters.</p>
<p>The film grossed over $1.02 billion worldwide, being Burton's most successful film to date, but received mixed reviews; although praised for its visual style, special effects and Johnny Depp's performance, the film was criticized for its lack of narrative, coherence and overuse of CGI. At the <a href="/wiki/83rd_Academy_Awards" title="83rd Academy Awards">83rd Academy Awards</a>, <i>Alice in Wonderland</i> won for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Art_Direction" title="Academy Award for Best Art Direction">Best Art Direction</a> and <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Costume_Design" title="Academy Award for Best Costume Design">Best Costume Design</a>, and was also nominated for <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Visual_Effects" title="Academy Award for Best Visual Effects">Best Visual Effects</a>. The film generated over $1 billion in ticket sales and, as of August 2014, it is the seventeenth <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_films" title="List of highest-grossing films">highest-grossing film of all time</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Time_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-Time-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> A sequel, titled <i><a href="/wiki/Alice_in_Wonderland:_Through_the_Looking_Glass" title="Alice in Wonderland: Through the Looking Glass">Alice in Wonderland: Through the Looking Glass</a></i>, is set for a May 27, 2016 release.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Plot">Plot</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alice_in_Wonderland_(2010_film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Plot">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Troubled by a strange recurring dream and mourning the loss of her beloved father, nineteen-year-old <a href="/wiki/Alice_(Alice%27s_Adventures_in_Wonderland)" title="Alice (Alice's Adventures in Wonderland)">Alice Kingsleigh</a> attends a garden party at Lord Ascot's estate, where she is confronted by an unwanted marriage proposal, to Hamish Ascot, and the stifling expectations of the society in which she lives. Unsure of how to reply, and increasingly confused, she runs away to chase after a rabbit in a blue waistcoat, and accidentally falls into a large rabbit hole. She is transported to a world called Underland, where she is greeted by the <a href="/wiki/White_Rabbit" title="White Rabbit">White Rabbit</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dormouse_(Alice%27s_Adventures_in_Wonderland)" title="Dormouse (Alice's Adventures in Wonderland)">Dormouse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dodo_(Alice%27s_Adventures_in_Wonderland)" title="Dodo (Alice's Adventures in Wonderland)">the Dodo</a>, the <a href="/wiki/List_of_minor_characters_in_the_Alice_series#Live_Flowers" title="List of minor characters in the Alice series">Talking Flowers</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tweedledee_and_Tweedledum" title="Tweedledee and Tweedledum">Tweedledee and Tweedledum</a>. They argue over her identity as "the right Alice", who it is foretold will slay the <a href="/wiki/Red_Queen_(Through_the_Looking-Glass)" title="Red Queen (Through the Looking-Glass)">Red Queen</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Jabberwocky" title="Jabberwocky">Jabberwocky</a> on the Frabjous Day and restore the <a href="/wiki/White_Queen_(Through_the_Looking-Glass)" title="White Queen (Through the Looking-Glass)">White Queen</a> to power as told by Absolem the <a href="/wiki/Caterpillar_(Alice%27s_Adventures_in_Wonderland)" title="Caterpillar (Alice's Adventures in Wonderland)">Caterpillar</a> and his Oraculum. The group is then ambushed by the <a href="/wiki/Bandersnatch" title="Bandersnatch">Bandersnatch</a> and a group of <a href="/wiki/List_of_minor_characters_in_the_Alice_series#The_Playing_Cards" title="List of minor characters in the Alice series">playing-card soldiers</a> led by the <a href="/wiki/Knave_of_Hearts_(Alice%27s_Adventures_in_Wonderland)" title="Knave of Hearts (Alice's Adventures in Wonderland)">Knave of Hearts</a> capturing the White Rabbit and the Dodo bird. Alice, Tweedledum and Tweedledee escape and flee into the woods, while the Knave steals the Oraculum and the Dormouse leaves the others with one of the Bandersnatch's eyes. Tweedledum and Tweedledee, however, were abducted by the Red Queen's Jubjub bird.</p>
<p>The Knave informs the Red Queen that Alice has returned and threatens her reign, and the soldiers and Bayard the <a href="/wiki/Bloodhound" title="Bloodhound">Bloodhound</a> are ordered to find Alice immediately. Meanwhile, the wandering Alice encounters the <a href="/wiki/Cheshire_Cat" title="Cheshire Cat">Cheshire Cat</a>, who takes her to the <a href="/wiki/March_Hare" title="March Hare">March Hare</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Hatter" title="The Hatter">the Hatter</a>. On the way to the White Queen's castle, Hatter relates the terror of the Red Queen's reign, and comments that Alice is not the same as she once was. The Hatter helps Alice avoid capture by allowing himself to be seized instead. Later, Alice is found by Bayard the Bloodhound, who wishes to take her to the White Queen (<a href="/wiki/Anne_Hathaway" title="Anne Hathaway">Anne Hathaway</a>), but Alice insists upon helping the Hatter, so they go to the Red Queen's castle.</p>
<p>The Red Queen is unaware of Alice's true identity and therefore welcomes her as a guest. Alice learns that the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vorpal_Sword" title="Vorpal Sword">Vorpal Sword</a>, the only weapon capable of killing the Jabberwocky, is locked away in a case inside the Bandersnatch's den. The Knave crudely attempts to seduce Alice, but she rebuffs him; a subordinate sees this and informs the Red Queen, but the Knave replies that Alice made advances on him instead, and a jealous Red Queen orders Alice beheaded. Alice later manages to retrieve the sword and befriend the Bandersnatch by returning its eye. The Knave finds her with the sword and attempts to arrest her. Alice escapes on the back of the Bandersnatch and delivers the sword to the White Queen. The Cheshire Cat saves the Hatter from the executioner, and the Hatter calls for rebellion against the Red Queen. The rebellion is quickly put down by the <a href="/wiki/Jubjub_bird" title="Jubjub bird">Jubjub bird</a>, but the resistance flees to the White Queen's castle, and both armies prepare for battle. Alice remains unsure about the expectation for her to champion the White Queen, and meets with a transforming Absolem. He reminds Alice of her past visit to Underland when she misheard the name of the place and called it "Wonderland" thirteen years earlier, and helps give her the courage to fight the Jabberwocky and accomplish "what she must to do" before completing his transformation into a <a href="/wiki/Pupa" title="Pupa">pupa</a>.</p>
<p>When the Frabjous Day arrives, both the White and Red Queens gather their massive armies on a <a href="/wiki/Chessboard" title="Chessboard">chessboard</a>-like battlefield and send forth their chosen champions (armor-clad Alice and the Jabberwocky respectively) to decide the fate of Underland. As Alice fights the Jabberwocky, the White and Red Queen's armies start battling each other, with the Red Queen's forces faltering. Encouraging herself with the words of her late father, Alice manages to behead the Jabberwocky, ending the battle. The White Queen then banishes her evil elder sister and the Knave to the Outlands; the Knave tries to kill the Red Queen but when he is stopped by the Hatter, he begs to be killed instead of banished, which the White Queen refuses. After the Hatter performs a celebration dance called Futterwacken, the White Queen gives Alice a vial of the Jabberwocky's purple blood, which will take her home. The Hatter suggests that she could stay in Underland, but she decides that she must go back and promises that she will return.</p>
<p>Alice returns home, where she stands up to her family and pledges to live her life on her own terms. Impressed, Lord Ascot takes her in as his apprentice with the idea of establishing oceanic <a href="/wiki/Trade_route" title="Trade route">trade routes</a> to China. As the story closes, Alice prepares to set off on a <a href="/wiki/Merchant_vessel" title="Merchant vessel">trading ship</a>. A light-blue butterfly lands on her shoulder, which Alice recognizes as Absolem and greets him before he flutters away.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cast">Cast</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alice_in_Wonderland_(2010_film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Cast">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mia_Wasikowska" title="Mia Wasikowska">Mia Wasikowska</a> as <a href="/wiki/Alice_(Alice%27s_Adventures_in_Wonderland)" title="Alice (Alice's Adventures in Wonderland)">Alice Kingsleigh</a>. When creating the character, screenwriter Linda Woolverton researched how young women were expected to behave in the Victorian era and then made her the opposite.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nytfeb2610_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-nytfeb2610-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> Wasikowska read Carroll's books as a child and re-read them to prepare for her role. She also watched <a href="/wiki/Jan_%C5%A0vankmajer" title="Jan Švankmajer">Jan Švankmajer</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Alice_(1988_film)" title="Alice (1988 film)">Alice</a></i>. She said, "When we were kids, my mum would pop it in the VCR player. We would be disturbed, and wouldn't really understand it, but we couldn't look away because it was too intriguing. So I had kept that feeling about Alice, a kind of haunting feeling."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SundayTimes_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-SundayTimes-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> Although facing pressures to conform to society's expectations, Alice grows into a stronger-willed and empowered heroine who chooses her own path; <i><a href="/wiki/The_Independent" title="The Independent">Independent</a></i> columnist Liz Hoggard praised Alice as a role model for girls, describing the character as "stubborn, brave, [and] non-girlie".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nytfeb2610_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-nytfeb2610-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> Mairi Ella Challen portrayed Alice as a six-year-old.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Johnny_Depp" title="Johnny Depp">Johnny Depp</a> as Tarrant Hightopp, <a href="/wiki/The_Hatter" title="The Hatter">The Mad Hatter</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-script_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-script-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> Wasikowska said that the characters "both feel like outsiders and feel alone in their separate worlds, and have a special bond and friendship."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.27.27Alice_in_Wonderland.27.27_star_Mia_Wasikowska_on_Johnny_Depp:_.27He.27s_so_brave_and_smart.27_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-.27.27Alice_in_Wonderland.27.27_star_Mia_Wasikowska_on_Johnny_Depp:_.27He.27s_so_brave_and_smart.27-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-confirm_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-confirm-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> Burton explained that Depp "tried to find a grounding to the character ... as opposed to just being mad."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sdcc09_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-sdcc09-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> Burton also said that, "In a lot of versions it's a very one-note kind of character and you know [Depp's] goal was to try and bring out a human side to the strangeness of the character."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sdcc09_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-sdcc09-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> The orange hair is an allusion to the <a href="/wiki/Mad_hatter_disease" title="Mad hatter disease">mercury poisoning suffered by hatters</a> who used mercury to cure felt; Depp believes that the character "was poisoned ... and it was coming out through his hair, through his fingernails and eyes".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Johnny_Depp_explains_how_he_picked_his_poison_with_the_Mad_Hatter_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-Johnny_Depp_explains_how_he_picked_his_poison_with_the_Mad_Hatter-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> Depp and Burton decided that the Hatter's clothes, skin, hair, personality and accent would change throughout the film to reflect his emotions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Johnny_Depp_is_Mad_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-Johnny_Depp_is_Mad-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> In an interview with Depp, the character was paralleled to "a <a href="/wiki/Mood_ring" title="Mood ring">mood ring</a>, [as] his emotions are <i>very</i> close to the surface".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Johnny_Depp_Sets_Sail_on_Fourth_.27.27Pirates.27.27_Movie_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-Johnny_Depp_Sets_Sail_on_Fourth_.27.27Pirates.27.27_Movie-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> The Hatter is <a href="/wiki/Dissociative_identity_disorder" title="Dissociative identity disorder">"made up of different people and their extreme sides"</a>, with a gentle voice much like the character's creator <a href="/wiki/Lewis_Carroll" title="Lewis Carroll">Lewis Carroll</a> reflecting the lighter personality and with a Scottish <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_patter" title="Glasgow patter">Glaswegian</a> accent (which Depp modeled after <a href="/wiki/Gregor_Fisher" title="Gregor Fisher">Gregor Fisher</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Rab_C._Nesbitt" title="Rab C. Nesbitt">Rab C. Nesbitt</a></i> character) reflecting a darker, more dangerous personality.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rab_C_Nesbitt_inspired_Mad_Hatter_accent_says_Johnny_Depp_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rab_C_Nesbitt_inspired_Mad_Hatter_accent_says_Johnny_Depp-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> Illusionary dancer <a href="/wiki/David_Bernal" title="David Bernal">David "Elsewhere" Bernal</a> doubled for Depp during the "Futterwacken" sequence near the end of the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Johnny_Depp.27s_body_double_and_other_.27Alice_in_Wonderland.27_secrets_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-Johnny_Depp.27s_body_double_and_other_.27Alice_in_Wonderland.27_secrets-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Queen_of_hearts_2010.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="248" data-file-width="402" height="154" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/d8/Queen_of_hearts_2010.jpg/250px-Queen_of_hearts_2010.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/d8/Queen_of_hearts_2010.jpg/375px-Queen_of_hearts_2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/d/d8/Queen_of_hearts_2010.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Queen_of_hearts_2010.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Helena Bonham Carter as the Red Queen. Bonham Carter's head was digitally increased to three times its original size in the film.</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Helena_Bonham_Carter" title="Helena Bonham Carter">Helena Bonham Carter</a> as Iracebeth of Crims, the Red Queen. She is an amalgamation of two Carroll characters: the <a href="/wiki/Red_Queen_(Through_the_Looking-Glass)" title="Red Queen (Through the Looking-Glass)">Red Queen</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Queen_of_Hearts_(Alice%27s_Adventures_in_Wonderland)" title="Queen of Hearts (Alice's Adventures in Wonderland)">Queen of Hearts</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-script_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-script-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> Her first name is a play on the word <a class="extiw" href="//en.wiktionary.org/wiki/irascible" title="wiktionary:irascible">irascible</a>, as she is easily irritated and quick to anger.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usatoday.com_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-usatoday.com-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> Bonham Carter's head was digitally increased to three times its original size on screen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-glove_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-glove-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-animation_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-animation-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> The character hates animals, choosing to use them as servants and furniture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Alice_in_Wonderland:_The_curious_one_that_will_get_the_kids_screaming..._23-0"><a href="#cite_note-Alice_in_Wonderland:_The_curious_one_that_will_get_the_kids_screaming...-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> The actress took inspiration from her young daughter Nell, a toddler, stating that, "The Red Queen is just like a toddler, because she's got a big head and she's a <a href="/wiki/Tyrant" title="Tyrant">tyrant</a>."</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Anne_Hathaway" title="Anne Hathaway">Anne Hathaway</a> as Mirana of Marmoreal, the <a href="/wiki/White_Queen_(Through_the_Looking-Glass)" title="White Queen (Through the Looking-Glass)">White Queen</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-script_11-2"><a href="#cite_note-script-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> She was one of few characters that did not require digital manipulation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tim_Burton_Takes_on_.27.27Alice_in_Wonderland.27.27_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tim_Burton_Takes_on_.27.27Alice_in_Wonderland.27.27-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> Hathaway summed up her character with a caption on a magnet of <a href="/wiki/It%27s_Happy_Bunny" title="It's Happy Bunny">Happy Bunny</a> holding a knife; "Cute but psycho. Things even out."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> According to Hathaway, "She comes from the same gene pool as the Red Queen. She really likes the dark side, but she's so scared of going too far into it that she's made everything appear very light and happy. But she's living in that place out of fear that she won't be able to control herself."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-darkside_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-darkside-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> Hathaway described her interpretation of the White Queen as "a <a href="/wiki/Punk_rock" title="Punk rock">punk-rock</a> <a href="/wiki/Veganism" title="Veganism">vegan</a> <a href="/wiki/Pacifism" title="Pacifism">pacifist</a>", with inspiration drawn from <a href="/wiki/Debbie_Harry" title="Debbie Harry">Debbie Harry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greta_Garbo" title="Greta Garbo">Greta Garbo</a>, and the artwork of <a href="/wiki/Dan_Flavin" title="Dan Flavin">Dan Flavin</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-darkside_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-darkside-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> Burton said that the White Queen's appearance was inspired by <a href="/wiki/Nigella_Lawson" title="Nigella Lawson">Nigella Lawson</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tim_Burton.27s_White_Queen_Based_on_Nigella_Lawson_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tim_Burton.27s_White_Queen_Based_on_Nigella_Lawson-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Crispin_Glover" title="Crispin Glover">Crispin Glover</a> played Ilosovic Stayne, the <a href="/wiki/Knave_of_Hearts_(Alice%27s_Adventures_in_Wonderland)" title="Knave of Hearts (Alice's Adventures in Wonderland)">Knave of Hearts</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-script_11-3"><a href="#cite_note-script-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> The character is arrogant and tricky, and while following the Red Queen's every order, he is the only one capable of calming her dramatic mood swings. Glover said, "The Red Queen has a fair amount of short-tempered reactions to things that people do, and so [the Knave] has to be quite diplomatic." The Red Queen believes he is her lover, but this proves this to be false.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Matt_Lucas" title="Matt Lucas">Matt Lucas</a> portrayed both <a href="/wiki/Tweedledum_and_Tweedledee" title="Tweedledum and Tweedledee">Tweedledee and Tweedledum</a>. Burton commented on the mixture of animation and Lucas, saying that "It's a weird mixture of things which gives his characters the disturbing quality that they so richly deserve."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> The characters are portrayed through a combination of CGI and live-action, with Lucas' face digitally composited to a full animated body. While performing the character, Lucas had to wear a teardrop-shaped motion capture suit and walk on stilts. In order to play both characters, Lucas was doubled by <a href="/wiki/Ethan_Cohn" title="Ethan Cohn">Ethan Cohn</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Frances_de_la_Tour" title="Frances de la Tour">Frances de la Tour</a> as Imogene, Alice's aunt.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Louisville_Mojo_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-Louisville_Mojo-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> She is suffering from severe delusions and is constantly awaiting her fictional fiancé whom she believes to be a prince</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Leo_Bill" title="Leo Bill">Leo Bill</a> as Hamish Ascot, the would-be fiancé of Alice.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Louisville_Mojo_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-Louisville_Mojo-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p><a href="/wiki/Marton_Csokas" title="Marton Csokas">Marton Csokas</a> makes a cameo appearance as Alice's deceased father in film's the opening scene and Alice's mother is played by <a href="/wiki/Lindsay_Duncan" title="Lindsay Duncan">Lindsay Duncan</a>. Lord and Lady Ascot are played by <a href="/wiki/Tim_Pigott-Smith" title="Tim Pigott-Smith">Tim Pigott-Smith</a> and <a href="/wiki/Geraldine_James" title="Geraldine James">Geraldine James</a> respectively. <a href="/wiki/Eleanor_Tomlinson" title="Eleanor Tomlinson">Eleanor Tomlinson</a> and Eleanor Gecks play the Cathaway sisters, who bear a strong resemblance to Tweedledum and Tweedledee. <a href="/wiki/Jemma_Powell" title="Jemma Powell">Jemma Powell</a> appears briefly as Alice's sister, Margaret, while Margaret's unfaithful husband Lowell is played by <a href="/wiki/John_Hopkins_(actor)" title="John Hopkins (actor)">John Hopkins</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Voice_Cast">Voice Cast</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alice_in_Wonderland_(2010_film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Voice Cast">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Michael_Sheen" title="Michael Sheen">Michael Sheen</a> voiced Nivens McTwisp, the <a href="/wiki/White_Rabbit" title="White Rabbit">White Rabbit</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-script_11-4"><a href="#cite_note-script-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Actor_Sheen_in_Wonderland_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-Actor_Sheen_in_Wonderland-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup> Sheen said the character "is such an iconic character that [he] didn't feel like [he] should break the mold too much."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Michael_Sheen_on_White_Rabbit_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-Michael_Sheen_on_White_Rabbit-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> Burton said the quality he wanted most in his clock-watching bunny was a twitchiness, also commenting that "[in] any incarnation of the [White Rabbit] through the years, there's that sort of nervousness of a rabbit."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Michael_Sheen_on_White_Rabbit_31-1"><a href="#cite_note-Michael_Sheen_on_White_Rabbit-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Alan_Rickman" title="Alan Rickman">Alan Rickman</a> voiced Absolem, the <a href="/wiki/Caterpillar_(Alice%27s_Adventures_in_Wonderland)" title="Caterpillar (Alice's Adventures in Wonderland)">Caterpillar</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-script_11-5"><a href="#cite_note-script-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> Rickman was originally going to have his face composited onto the animated Caterpillar. He was filmed recording his voice in the studio, but the idea was eventually scrapped. The animators did, however, try to give Absolem's face characteristics similar to Rickman's.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-animation_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-animation-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Barbara_Windsor" title="Barbara Windsor">Barbara Windsor</a> voiced Mallymkun, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dormouse_(Alice%27s_Adventures_in_Wonderland)" title="Dormouse (Alice's Adventures in Wonderland)">Dormouse</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-script_11-6"><a href="#cite_note-script-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> Burton said that he sought after Windsor for the role because he was a fan of her TV show <i><a href="/wiki/EastEnders" title="EastEnders">EastEnders</a></i>. Her voice sealed the deal for her role as the character.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Stephen_Fry" title="Stephen Fry">Stephen Fry</a> voiced Cheshire, the <a href="/wiki/Cheshire_Cat" title="Cheshire Cat">Cheshire Cat</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-script_11-7"><a href="#cite_note-script-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Five_Minutes_With:_Stephen_Fry_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-Five_Minutes_With:_Stephen_Fry-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> Burton stated that the character had a creepy quality in addition to tapping into his own hatred of cats.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-daily_cast_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-daily_cast-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Cheshire_Cat_taps_into...my_hatred_of_cats_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_Cheshire_Cat_taps_into...my_hatred_of_cats-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> The role was intended to be played by Michael Sheen but he changed his role to the White Rabbit due to scheduling conflicts.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Paul_Whitehouse" title="Paul Whitehouse">Paul Whitehouse</a> voiced Thackery Earwicket, the <a href="/wiki/March_Hare" title="March Hare">March Hare</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-script_11-8"><a href="#cite_note-script-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> Burton stated that because Whitehouse is a great comedic actor, a lot of his lines came from <a href="/wiki/Improvisation" title="Improvisation">improvisation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Alice_in_Wonderland:_A_Visual_Companion_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-Alice_in_Wonderland:_A_Visual_Companion-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Timothy_Spall" title="Timothy Spall">Timothy Spall</a> voiced Bayard, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Puppy_(Alice%27s_Adventures_in_Wonderland)" title="The Puppy (Alice's Adventures in Wonderland)">Bloodhound</a>. Although Bayard does not appear in the book, a similar character named The Puppy is likely the inspiration for the character.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Michael_Gough" title="Michael Gough">Michael Gough</a> voiced Uilleam, the <a href="/wiki/Dodo_(Alice%27s_Adventures_in_Wonderland)" title="Dodo (Alice's Adventures in Wonderland)">Dodo</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-script_11-9"><a href="#cite_note-script-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> Burton said that Gough was the first person he thought of for the role of the Dodo because he has "a full life quality to his voice".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Alice_in_Wonderland:_A_Visual_Companion1_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-Alice_in_Wonderland:_A_Visual_Companion1-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> The character only speaks three lines, that Gough recorded in a day. Unfortunately, this would be Gough's final acting role where he passed away the following year aged 94. Gough had previously portrayed the March Hare in the <a href="/wiki/Alice_in_Wonderland_(1966_TV_play)" title="Alice in Wonderland (1966 TV play)">1966 TV play</a> of the book.</li>
<li>Sir <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Lee" title="Christopher Lee">Christopher Lee</a> voiced the <a href="/wiki/Jabberwocky" title="Jabberwocky">Jabberwocky</a>. While it only had two lines, Burton said that he felt Lee to be a good match for the iconic character because he is "an iconic guy".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Alice_in_Wonderland:_A_Visual_Companion2_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-Alice_in_Wonderland:_A_Visual_Companion2-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> For the character, Lee had originally tried to make his voice 'burble' (as described in the poem "Jabberwocky"). However, Tim Burton convinced him to use his actual voice, as he found it more intimidating.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Imelda_Staunton" title="Imelda Staunton">Imelda Staunton</a> voiced all three of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_minor_characters_in_the_Alice_series#Live_Flowers" title="List of minor characters in the Alice series">Talking Flowers</a>. Though there are many flowers that appear around Wonderland, only three of them speak and one of them is clearly a <a href="/wiki/Caricature" title="Caricature">caricature</a> of Staunton.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-presskit_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-presskit-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup> Staunton only speaks three lines that are heard very briefly at the beginning of the film.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jim_Carter_(actor)" title="Jim Carter (actor)">Jim Carter</a> voiced the <a href="/wiki/List_of_minor_characters_in_the_Alice_series#Executioner" title="List of minor characters in the Alice series">Red Queen's executioner</a>. The Executioner only speaks one line and appears extremely briefly, though Carter also voiced several other servants to the Red Queen.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Frank_Welker" title="Frank Welker">Frank Welker</a> provided additional voices and vocal effects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-presskit_39-1"><a href="#cite_note-presskit-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p>Rickman, Windsor, Fry, Gough, Lee, Staunton and Carter each took only a day to record their dialogue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-presskit_39-2"><a href="#cite_note-presskit-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Production">Production</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alice_in_Wonderland_(2010_film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Production">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/Tim_Burton" title="Tim Burton">Tim Burton</a> signed with <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Pictures" title="Walt Disney Pictures">Walt Disney Pictures</a> to direct two films in <a href="/wiki/Disney_Digital_3-D" title="Disney Digital 3-D">Disney Digital 3D</a>, which included <i>Alice in Wonderland</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Graser_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-Graser-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Frankenweenie_(2012_film)" title="Frankenweenie (2012 film)">his remake of <i>Frankenweenie</i></a>. Burton developed the story because he never felt an emotional tie to <a href="/wiki/Alice%27s_Adventures_in_Wonderland" title="Alice's Adventures in Wonderland">the original book</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ryder_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ryder-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>He explained "the goal is to try to make it an engaging movie where you get some of the psychology and kind of bring a freshness but also keep the classic nature of <i>Alice</i>." On prior versions, Burton said "It was always a girl wandering around from one crazy character to another, and I never really felt any real emotional connection." His goal with the new movie is to give the story "some framework of emotional grounding" and "to try and make <i>Alice</i> feel more like a story as opposed to a series of events."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sdcc09_14-2"><a href="#cite_note-sdcc09-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> Burton focused on the poem "<a href="/wiki/Jabberwocky" title="Jabberwocky">Jabberwocky</a>" as part of his structure,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup> and refers to the described creature by the name of the poem rather than by the name "Jabberwock" used in the poem. Burton also stated that he does not see his version as either a sequel to any existing <i>Alice</i> film nor as a "re-imagining".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ryder_41-1"><a href="#cite_note-Ryder-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> However, the idea of the climax of the story being Alice's battle with the Queen's champion, the Jabberwocky, was first added in the video game <a href="/wiki/American_McGee%27s_Alice" title="American McGee's Alice">American McGee's Alice</a>, and the landscape, tower, and weapons and appearance of Alice in those scenes of the movie are very reminiscent of the same scenes in the game.</p>
<table cellspacing="5" class="toccolours" style="float: right; margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 2em; font-size: 95%; color:black; width:25em; max-width: 40%;">
<tr>
<td style="text-align: left;">We wanted somebody who had... it's hard to put into words, but just had a gravity to her, an internal life, something that you could see the wheels turning. It's just a simple kind of power to her that we really liked. Not flamboyant, not very showy, but just somebody that's got a lot of internal life to her. That's why I picked her.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td style="text-align: left;">—Burton on casting <a href="/wiki/Mia_Wasikowska" title="Mia Wasikowska">Mia Wasikowska</a> as Alice<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tim_Burton_Interview_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tim_Burton_Interview-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>This film was originally set to be released in 2009, but was pushed back to March 5, 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Disney_unveils_2009_schedule_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-Disney_unveils_2009_schedule-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Principal_photography" title="Principal photography">Principal photography</a> was scheduled for May 2008, but did not begin until September and concluded in three months.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Graser_40-1"><a href="#cite_note-Graser-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-firstlook_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-firstlook-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> Scenes set in the <a href="/wiki/Victorian_era" title="Victorian era">Victorian era</a> were shot at <a href="/wiki/Torpoint" title="Torpoint">Torpoint</a> and <a href="/wiki/Plymouth" title="Plymouth">Plymouth</a> from September 1 to October 14. Two hundred and fifty local <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extra_(actor)" title="Extra (actor)">extras</a> were chosen in early August. Locations included <a href="/wiki/Antony_House" title="Antony House">Antony House</a> in Torpoint, <a href="/wiki/Charlestown,_Cornwall" title="Charlestown, Cornwall">Charlestown, Cornwall</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barbican,_Plymouth" title="Barbican, Plymouth">the Barbican</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Burton_brings_Hollywood_to_Cornwall_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-Burton_brings_Hollywood_to_Cornwall-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Plymouth_in_Wonderland_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-Plymouth_in_Wonderland-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> however, no footage from the Barbican was used. <a href="/wiki/Motion_capture" title="Motion capture">Motion capture</a> filming began in early October at <a href="/wiki/Sony_Pictures_Studios" title="Sony Pictures Studios">Sony Pictures Studios</a> in Culver City, California, though the footage was later discarded.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Comic_Lucas_reveals_movie_plans_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-Comic_Lucas_reveals_movie_plans-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-On_The_Set_of_Alice_In_Wonderland_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-On_The_Set_of_Alice_In_Wonderland-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup> Filming also took place at <a href="/wiki/Culver_Studios" title="Culver Studios">Culver Studios</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Alan_Rickman_Interview_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-Alan_Rickman_Interview-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> Burton said that he used a combination of live action and animation, without motion capture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-explores_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-explores-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> He also noted that this was the first time he had filmed on a <a href="/wiki/Chroma_key" title="Chroma key">green screen</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-explores_52-1"><a href="#cite_note-explores-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> Filming of the green screen portions, comprising 90% of the film, was completed after only 40 days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-telegraph100215_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph100215-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> Many of the cast and crew felt nauseated as a result of the long hours surrounded by green, with Burton having lavender lenses fitted into his glasses to counteract the effect.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-telegraph100215_53-1"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph100215-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> Due to the constant need for digital effects to distort the actors' physical appearances, such as the size of the Red Queen's head or Alice's height, visual effects supervisor <a href="/wiki/Ken_Ralston" title="Ken Ralston">Ken Ralston</a> cited the film as being exhausting, saying it was "The biggest show I've ever done, [and] the most creatively involved I've ever been."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Down_the_Rabbit_Hole_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-Down_the_Rabbit_Hole-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Sony_Pictures_Imageworks" title="Sony Pictures Imageworks">Sony Pictures Imageworks</a> designed the visual effects sequences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Johnny_Depp_in_deep_with_Disney_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-Johnny_Depp_in_deep_with_Disney-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup> Burton felt 3D was appropriate to the story's environment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-confirm_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-confirm-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> Burton and Zanuck chose to film with conventional cameras, and <a href="/wiki/2D_to_3D_conversion" title="2D to 3D conversion">convert</a> the footage into 3D during post-production; Zanuck explained 3D cameras were too expensive and "clumsy" to use, and they felt that there was no difference between converted footage and those shot in the format.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Richard_Zanuck_and_James_Cameron_spar_over_Alice_in_Wonderland_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-Richard_Zanuck_and_James_Cameron_spar_over_Alice_in_Wonderland-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/James_Cameron" title="James Cameron">James Cameron</a>, who released his 3D film <i><a href="/wiki/Avatar_(2009_film)" title="Avatar (2009 film)">Avatar</a></i> in December 2009, criticized the choice, stating, "It doesn't make any sense to shoot in 2-D and convert to 3-D".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-James_Cameron_Criticizes_Tim_Burton_and_3D_DVD_Releases_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-James_Cameron_Criticizes_Tim_Burton_and_3D_DVD_Releases-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alice_in_Wonderland_(2010_film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Score">Score</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alice_in_Wonderland_(2010_film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Score">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Template:Infobhjjh&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Template:Infobhjjh (page does not exist)">Template:Infobhjjh</a> Longtime Burton collaborator <a href="/wiki/Danny_Elfman" title="Danny Elfman">Danny Elfman</a>'s score was released March 2, 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-earthtimes_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-earthtimes-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup> It debuted at #89 on the <i>Billboard</i> Top 200 albums chart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Week_Ending_March_7.2C_2010:_Cruz_Controls_Hot_100_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-Week_Ending_March_7.2C_2010:_Cruz_Controls_Hot_100-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Almost_Alice"><i>Almost Alice</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alice_in_Wonderland_(2010_film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Almost Alice">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Almost_Alice" title="Almost Alice">Almost Alice</a></div>
<p><i>Almost Alice</i> is a collection of various artists' music inspired by the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-earthtimes_58-1"><a href="#cite_note-earthtimes-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Avril_Lavigne_Song_To_Appear_On_Tim_Burton.27s_.27.27Alice_In_Wonderland.27.27_Soundtrack_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-Avril_Lavigne_Song_To_Appear_On_Tim_Burton.27s_.27.27Alice_In_Wonderland.27.27_Soundtrack-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tokio_Hotel_And_Kerli_Will_Collaborate_On_Tim_Burton.27s_.27.27Alice_In_Wonderland.27.27_Soundtrack_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tokio_Hotel_And_Kerli_Will_Collaborate_On_Tim_Burton.27s_.27.27Alice_In_Wonderland.27.27_Soundtrack-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Lead_single" title="Lead single">lead single</a>, "<a href="/wiki/Alice_(Avril_Lavigne_song)" title="Alice (Avril Lavigne song)">Alice</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Avril_Lavigne" title="Avril Lavigne">Avril Lavigne</a>, premiered on January 27, 2010 on <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Seacrest" title="Ryan Seacrest">Ryan Seacrest</a>'s radio program. Other singles include "Follow Me Down" by <a href="/wiki/3OH!3" title="3OH!3">3OH!3</a>, "Her Name Is Alice" by <a href="/wiki/Shinedown" title="Shinedown">Shinedown</a>, and "Tea Party" by <a href="/wiki/Kerli" title="Kerli">Kerli</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Interview_with_Avril_Lavigne_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-Interview_with_Avril_Lavigne-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> The album was released on March 2, 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-earthtimes_58-2"><a href="#cite_note-earthtimes-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Release">Release</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alice_in_Wonderland_(2010_film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Release">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>On February 12, 2010, major UK cinema chains, <a href="/wiki/Odeon_Cinemas" title="Odeon Cinemas">Odeon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vue_Cinemas" title="Vue Cinemas">Vue</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cineworld" title="Cineworld">Cineworld</a>, had planned to boycott the film because of a reduction of the interval between cinema and DVD <a href="/wiki/Film_release" title="Film release">release</a> from the usual 17 weeks to 12.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup> A week after the announcement, Cineworld, who has a 24% share of UK box office, chose to play the film on more than 150 screens. Cineworld's chief executive Steve Wiener stated, "As leaders in 3D, we did not want the public to miss out on such a visual spectacle. As the success of <i>Avatar</i> has shown, there is currently a huge appetite for the 3D experience".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cineworld_backs_off_from_Alice_in_Wonderland_boycott_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cineworld_backs_off_from_Alice_in_Wonderland_boycott-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup> Shortly after, the Vue cinema chain also reached an agreement with Disney, but Odeon had still chosen to boycott in Britain, Ireland and Italy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-odeon_boycott_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-odeon_boycott-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup> On February 25, 2010 Odeon had reached an agreement and decided to show the film on March 5, 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Odeon_makes_U-turn_on_.27.27Alice.27.27_boycott_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-Odeon_makes_U-turn_on_.27.27Alice.27.27_boycott-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> The Royal premiere took place at the <a href="/wiki/Odeon_Leicester_Square" title="Odeon Leicester Square">Odeon Leicester Square</a> in London on February 25, 2010 for the fundraiser <a href="/wiki/The_Prince%27s_Foundation_for_Children_and_The_Arts" title="The Prince's Foundation for Children and The Arts">The Prince's Foundation for Children and The Arts</a> where the <a href="/wiki/Charles,_Prince_of_Wales" title="Charles, Prince of Wales">Prince of Wales</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Camilla,_Duchess_of_Cornwall" title="Camilla, Duchess of Cornwall">Duchess of Cornwall</a> attended. It also did not affect their plans to show the film in Spain, Germany, <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-odeon_boycott_65-1"><a href="#cite_note-odeon_boycott-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-A_very_important_date:_.27.27Alice_in_Wonderland.27.27_will_premiere_in_London_on_Feb._25_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-A_very_important_date:_.27.27Alice_in_Wonderland.27.27_will_premiere_in_London_on_Feb._25-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Johnny_Depp_greets_fans_at_Alice_In_Wonderland_premiere_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-Johnny_Depp_greets_fans_at_Alice_In_Wonderland_premiere-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> The film was released in the U.S. and UK, in both <a href="/wiki/Disney_Digital_3-D" title="Disney Digital 3-D">Disney Digital 3D</a> and <a href="/wiki/IMAX" title="IMAX">IMAX 3D</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-firstlook_45-1"><a href="#cite_note-firstlook-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> as well as regular theaters on March 5, 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Marketing">Marketing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alice_in_Wonderland_(2010_film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Marketing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:177px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:DCA_Mad_T_Party_Dormouse_jump.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4608" data-file-width="3456" height="233" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/DCA_Mad_T_Party_Dormouse_jump.jpg/175px-DCA_Mad_T_Party_Dormouse_jump.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/DCA_Mad_T_Party_Dormouse_jump.jpg/263px-DCA_Mad_T_Party_Dormouse_jump.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/DCA_Mad_T_Party_Dormouse_jump.jpg/350px-DCA_Mad_T_Party_Dormouse_jump.jpg 2x" width="175"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:DCA_Mad_T_Party_Dormouse_jump.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Mad T Party at California Adventure, showing the Dormouse on guitar, Cheshire Cat on drums, and Alice as lead singer.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On June 22, 2009, the first pictures of the film were released, showing Depp as the Mad Hatter, Hathaway as the White Queen, Bonham Carter as the Red Queen and Lucas as Tweedledee and Tweedledum.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-firstlook_45-2"><a href="#cite_note-firstlook-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> A new image of Alice was also released.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.27.27Alice_in_Wonderland.27.27_Stills_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-.27.27Alice_in_Wonderland.27.27_Stills-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup> In July, new photos emerged of Alice holding a white rabbit, the Mad Hatter with a hare, the Red Queen holding a pig, and the White Queen with a mouse.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Exclusive:_New_Alice_In_Wonderland_Pic_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-Exclusive:_New_Alice_In_Wonderland_Pic-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On July 22, 2009, a <a href="/wiki/Teaser_campaign" title="Teaser campaign">teaser trailer</a> from the Mad Hatter's point of view was released on <a href="/wiki/IGN" title="IGN">IGN</a> but was shortly taken down because Disney claimed that the trailer was not supposed to be out yet. The teaser was also planned to premiere along with a trailer of <a href="/wiki/Robert_Zemeckis" title="Robert Zemeckis">Robert Zemeckis</a>' <a href="/wiki/Film_adaptation" title="Film adaptation">film adaptation</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/A_Christmas_Carol_(2009_film)" title="A Christmas Carol (2009 film)">A Christmas Carol</a></i> on July 24, 2009 for <i><a href="/wiki/G-Force_(film)" title="G-Force (film)">G-Force</a></i>. The following day, the teaser trailer premiered at <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Comic-Con_International" title="San Diego Comic-Con International">Comic-Con</a> but the trailer shown was different from the one that leaked. The ComicCon version didn't have the Mad Hatter's dialogue. Instead, it featured "<a href="/wiki/Time_to_Pretend" title="Time to Pretend">Time to Pretend</a>" by <a href="/wiki/MGMT" title="MGMT">MGMT</a>, and the clips shown were in different order than in the leaked version. The leaked version was originally to be shown to one of the three Facebook groups used to promote the film that had the most members. The groups used to promote the film are "The Loyal Subjects of the Red Queen", "The Loyal Subjects of the White Queen" and "The Disloyal Subjects of the Mad Hatter".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Also at ComicCon, <a href="/wiki/Theatrical_property" title="Theatrical property">props</a> from the film were displayed in an "Alice in Wonderland" exhibit. Costumes featured in the exhibit included the Red Queen's dress, chair, wig, spectacles and scepter; the White Queen's dress, wig and a small model of her castle; the Mad Hatter's suit, hat, wig, chair and table; Alice's dress and battle armor (to slay the Jabberwocky). Other props included the "DRINK ME" bottles, the keys, an "EAT ME" pastry and stand-in models of the White Rabbit and March Hare.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Alice_in_Wonderland_Props_Totally_Rock_at_Comic_Con_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-Alice_in_Wonderland_Props_Totally_Rock_at_Comic_Con-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>A nighttime party area at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Disney%27s_California_Adventure" title="Disney's California Adventure">Disney's California Adventure</a> theme park was created, called "<a href="/wiki/Mad_T_Party" title="Mad T Party">Mad T Party</a>".</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Video_game">Video game</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alice_in_Wonderland_(2010_film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Video game">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Alice_in_Wonderland_(2010_video_game)" title="Alice in Wonderland (2010 video game)">Alice in Wonderland (2010 video game)</a></div>
<p>On July 23, 2009, <a href="/wiki/Disney_Interactive_Studios" title="Disney Interactive Studios">Disney Interactive Studios</a> announced that an <i>Alice in Wonderland</i> video game, developed by French game studio <a href="/wiki/%C3%89tranges_Libellules" title="Étranges Libellules">Étranges Libellules</a>, would be released in the same week as the film for the <a href="/wiki/Wii" title="Wii">Wii</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nintendo_DS" title="Nintendo DS">Nintendo DS</a> and <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Windows" title="Microsoft Windows">Microsoft Windows</a>, with the soundtrack being composed by veteran video games music composer <a href="/wiki/Richard_Jacques" title="Richard Jacques">Richard Jacques</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Illusion.2C_magic_and_impossible_ideas_come_to_life_in_upcoming_Alice_in_Wonderland_video_games_from_Disney_Interactive_Studios_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-Illusion.2C_magic_and_impossible_ideas_come_to_life_in_upcoming_Alice_in_Wonderland_video_games_from_Disney_Interactive_Studios-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup> The Wii, DS and PC versions were released on March 2, 2010.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Home_media">Home media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alice_in_Wonderland_(2010_film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Home media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Studios_Home_Entertainment" title="Walt Disney Studios Home Entertainment">Walt Disney Studios Home Entertainment</a> released a 3-disc <a href="/wiki/Blu-ray_Disc" title="Blu-ray Disc">Blu-ray</a> combo pack (which includes the Blu-ray, DVD and a <a href="/wiki/Digital_copy" title="Digital copy">digital copy</a>), 1-disc Blu-ray and 1-disc DVD on June 1, 2010 in the US and July 1, 2010 in Australia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Alice_in_Wonderland_.282010.29_on_DVD_at_dstore_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-Alice_in_Wonderland_.282010.29_on_DVD_at_dstore-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> All versions are presented in <a href="/wiki/1080p" title="1080p">1080p</a> with a 16:9 <a href="/wiki/Aspect_ratio_(image)" title="Aspect ratio (image)">aspect ratio</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dolby_Digital" title="Dolby Digital">Dolby Digital</a> 5.1 HD surround sound. The DVD release includes three short features about the making of the film, focusing on Burton's vision for Wonderland and the characters of Alice and the Mad Hatter. The Blu-ray version has nine additional featurettes centered on additional characters, special effects and other aspects of the film's production.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> In some confusion, a small number of copies were put on shelves a week before schedule in smaller stores, but were quickly removed, although a handful of copies were confirmed purchased ahead of schedule.</p>
<p>In its first week of release (June 1–6, 2010), it sold 2,095,878 DVD units (equivalent to $35,441,297) and topped the DVD sales chart for two continuous weeks. By May 22, 2011, it had sold 4,313,680 units ($76,413,043). It failed to crack the 2010 top ten DVDs list in terms of units sold, but reached 10th place on that chart in terms of sales revenue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reception">Reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alice_in_Wonderland_(2010_film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Box_office">Box office</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alice_in_Wonderland_(2010_film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Box office">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i>Alice in Wonderland</i> earned $334,191,110 in North America, as of July 8, 2010, and $691,276,000 in other territories, as of July 10, 2011, for a worldwide total of $1,025,467,110.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BOM_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-BOM-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Alice_in_Wonderland_Daily_Box_Office_Results_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-Alice_in_Wonderland_Daily_Box_Office_Results-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.27.27Alice_in_Wonderland.27.27_opens_strongly_at_box_office_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-.27.27Alice_in_Wonderland.27.27_opens_strongly_at_box_office-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup> Worldwide, it is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_films#Highest-grossing_films" title="List of highest-grossing films">seventeenth highest-grossing film</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-All_Time_Worldwide_Box_Office_Grosses_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-All_Time_Worldwide_Box_Office_Grosses-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/2010_in_film#Highest-grossing_films" title="2010 in film">second highest-grossing 2010 film</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2010_Worldwide_Grosses_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-2010_Worldwide_Grosses-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup> It is the third highest-grossing film starring <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Depp" title="Johnny Depp">Johnny Depp</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Johnny_Depp_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-Johnny_Depp-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup> the highest-grossing film directed by <a href="/wiki/Tim_Burton" title="Tim Burton">Tim Burton</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TimB_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-TimB-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> and the second highest-grossing children's book adaptation (worldwide, as well as in North America and outside North America separately).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On its first weekend, the film made $220.1 million worldwide, marking the second-largest opening ever for a movie not released during the summer or the holiday period (behind <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hunger_Games_(film)" title="The Hunger Games (film)">The Hunger Games</a></i>), the fourth largest for a Disney film and the fourth largest among 2010 films.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup> It dominated for three consecutive weekends at the worldwide box office.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Top_Grossing_Movies_in_Their_3rd_Weekend_at_the_Box_Office_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-Top_Grossing_Movies_in_Their_3rd_Weekend_at_the_Box_Office-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Top_Grossing_Movies_in_Their_2nd_Weekend_at_the_Box_Office_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-Top_Grossing_Movies_in_Their_2nd_Weekend_at_the_Box_Office-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup> On May 26, 2010, its 85th day of release, it became the sixth film ever to surpass the $1-billion-mark and the second film produced and released by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Motion_Pictures_Group" title="Walt Disney Motion Pictures Group">Walt Disney Studios</a> that did so.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>North America</dt>
</dl>
<p><i>Alice in Wonderland</i> is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_films_in_Canada_and_the_United_States#Not_adjusted_for_inflation" title="List of highest-grossing films in Canada and the United States">twenty-eighth highest-grossing film</a> but out of the top 100 when <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_films_in_Canada_and_the_United_States#Adjusted_for_ticket-price_inflation" title="List of highest-grossing films in Canada and the United States">adjusted for inflation</a>. It is also the <a href="/wiki/2010_in_film#Highest-grossing_films" title="2010 in film">second highest-grossing 2010 film</a>, behind <i><a href="/wiki/Toy_Story_3" title="Toy Story 3">Toy Story 3</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2010_Yearly_Box_Office_Results_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-2010_Yearly_Box_Office_Results-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup> the second highest-grossing film starring Johnny Depp<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Johnny_Depp_83-1"><a href="#cite_note-Johnny_Depp-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup> and the highest-grossing film directed by Tim Burton.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TimB_84-1"><a href="#cite_note-TimB-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> The film opened on March 5, 2010, on approximately 7,400 screens at 3,728 theaters with $40,804,962 during its first day, $3.9 million of which came from midnight showings,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup> ranking number one and setting a new March opening-day record.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Alice</i> earned $116.1 million on its opening weekend, breaking the record for the largest opening weekend in March (previously held by <i><a href="/wiki/300_(film)" title="300 (film)">300</a></i>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Top_March_Opening_Weekends_at_the_Box_Office_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-Top_March_Opening_Weekends_at_the_Box_Office-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> the record for the largest opening weekend during springtime (previously held by <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fast_%26_Furious" title="Fast &amp; Furious">Fast and Furious</a></i>), the largest opening weekend for a non-sequel (previously held by <i><a href="/wiki/Spider-Man_(2002_film)" title="Spider-Man (2002 film)">Spider-Man</a></i>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Biggest_Opening_Weekends_at_the_Box_Office_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-Biggest_Opening_Weekends_at_the_Box_Office-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup> and the highest one for the non-holiday, non-summer period. However, all of these records were broken by <i>The Hunger Games</i> ($152.5 million) in March 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Box_Office_Mojo_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-Box_Office_Mojo-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Alice</i> made the seventeenth highest-grossing opening weekend ever<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup> and the fifth largest among 3D films.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup> Opening-weekend grosses originating from 3D showings were $81.3 million (70% of total weekend gross). This broke the record for the largest opening-weekend 3D grosses<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boxofficemojo1_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-boxofficemojo1-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup> but it was topped by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Avengers_(2012_film)" title="The Avengers (2012 film)">Marvel's The Avengers</a></i> ($108 million).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BOM-Avengers_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-BOM-Avengers-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup> It had the largest weekend per theater average of 2010 ($31,143 per theater) and the largest for a PG-rated film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup> It broke the <a href="/wiki/IMAX" title="IMAX">IMAX</a> opening-weekend record<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup> by earning $12.2 million on 188 IMAX screens, with an average of $64,197 per site. The record was first overtaken by <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Deathly_Hallows_%E2%80%93_Part_2" title="Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows – Part 2">Deathly Hallows – Part 2</a></i> ($15.2 million).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boxofficemojo1_103-1"><a href="#cite_note-boxofficemojo1-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Alice</i> remained in first place for three consecutive weekends at the North American box office.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Alice</i> closed in theaters on July 8, 2010 with $334.2 million.</p>
<dl>
<dt>Outside North America</dt>
</dl>
<p>Outside North America, <i>Alice</i> is the thirteenth highest-grossing film,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup> the highest-grossing 2010 film,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup> the fourth highest-grossing Disney film, the second highest-grossing film starring Johnny Depp<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Johnny_Depp_83-2"><a href="#cite_note-Johnny_Depp-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup> and the highest-grossing film directed by Tim Burton.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TimB_84-2"><a href="#cite_note-TimB-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> It began with an estimated $94 million, on top of the weekend box office, and remained at the summit for four consecutive weekends and five in total.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup> Japan was the film's highest-grossing country after North America, with $133.7 million, followed by the UK, Ireland and Malta ($64.4 million), and France and the Maghreb region ($45.9 million).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Critical_reaction">Critical reaction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alice_in_Wonderland_(2010_film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Critical reaction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The film received mixed reviews. Review aggregate <a href="/wiki/Rotten_Tomatoes" title="Rotten Tomatoes">Rotten Tomatoes</a> reports that 51% of critics have given the film a positive review based on 263 reviews, with an average score of 5.7/10 and the consensus "Tim Burton's <i>Alice</i> sacrifices the book's minimal narrative coherence -- and much of its heart -- but it's an undeniable visual treat.".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Alice_in_Wonderland_.282010.293_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-Alice_in_Wonderland_.282010.293-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Metacritic" title="Metacritic">Metacritic</a>, which assigns a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Weighted_average" title="Weighted average">weighted average</a> score out of 1–100 reviews from film critics, has a rating score of 53 based on 38 reviews.</p>
<p>Todd McCarthy of <i><a href="/wiki/Variety_(magazine)" title="Variety (magazine)">Variety</a></i> praised it for its "moments of delight, humor and bedazzlement", but went on to say, "But it also becomes more ordinary as it goes along, building to a generic battle climax similar to any number of others in CGI-heavy movies of the past few years".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Alice_in_Wonderland_Review_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-Alice_in_Wonderland_Review-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup> Michael Rechtshaffen of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hollywood_Reporter" title="The Hollywood Reporter">The Hollywood Reporter</a></i> said "Burton has delivered a subversively witty, brilliantly cast, whimsically appointed dazzler that also manages to hit all the emotionally satisfying marks", while as well praising its <a href="/wiki/Computer-generated_imagery" title="Computer-generated imagery">computer-generated imagery</a> (CGI), saying "Ultimately, it's the visual landscape that makes Alice's newest adventure so wondrous, as technology has finally been able to catch up with Burton's endlessly fertile imagination."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Owen_Gleiberman" title="Owen Gleiberman">Owen Gleiberman</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a></i> said, "But Burton's Disneyfied 3-D <i>Alice in Wonderland</i>, written by the girl-power specialist Linda Woolverton, is a strange brew indeed: murky, diffuse, and meandering, set not in a Wonderland that pops with demented life but in a world called Underland that's like a joyless, bombed-out version of Wonderland. It looks like a CGI head trip gone post apocalyptic. In the film's rather humdrum 3-D, the place doesn't dazzle — it droops."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Roger_Ebert" title="Roger Ebert">Roger Ebert</a> of the <i><a href="/wiki/Chicago_Sun-Times" title="Chicago Sun-Times">Chicago Sun-Times</a></i> awarded the film three out of four stars and said in his review that, "<i>Alice</i> plays better as an adult hallucination, which is how Burton rather brilliantly interprets it until a pointless third act flies off the rails."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Alice_in_Wonderland_Review4_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-Alice_in_Wonderland_Review4-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup> The market research firm <a href="/wiki/CinemaScore" title="CinemaScore">CinemaScore</a> found that audiences gave the film an average rating of "A-".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Several reviews criticized the decision to turn Alice into a "colonialist entrepreneur" at the end of the film setting sail for China.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Alice_in_Wonderland_review_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-Alice_in_Wonderland_review-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.27.27Alice_in_Wonderland_in_Digital_3-D.27.27_clowns_paying_audience_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-.27.27Alice_in_Wonderland_in_Digital_3-D.27.27_clowns_paying_audience-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Alice_in_Wonderland_review5_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-Alice_in_Wonderland_review5-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup> Given Britain's role in the <a href="/wiki/First_Opium_War" title="First Opium War">First</a> and <a href="/wiki/Second_Opium_War" title="Second Opium War">Second Opium Wars</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Victorian_era" title="Victorian era">Victorian era</a> and the subjugation of China through "<a href="/wiki/Unequal_treaty" title="Unequal treaty">unequal treaties</a>", China expert Kevin Slaten writes, "Not only is it troubling imagery for a female role model in a Disney movie, but it's also a celebration of the exploitation that China suffered for a century."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Who_else_might_be_mad_at_Alice.3F_China_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-Who_else_might_be_mad_at_Alice.3F_China-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
